Replay is deterministic, cancellable, and bounded to prevent runaway loops, with clear post-run summaries of actions applied.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>COMP-6</td> <td>Two-pane split editing and compare-grade navigation</td> <td>Features</td> <td>M</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>QUILL adds an optional split editing mode that keeps stock controls and predictable focus semantics, with explicit announcements for pane entry, active pane, and synchronized navigation state. Users can open two files or two positions of one file, lock or unlock scroll, and drive pane focus and movement entirely by keyboard. The feature reuses compare navigation primitives so jumps, hunk traversal, and region review remain coherent and screen-reader friendly.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr /> <h2 id="15-suggested-release-sequencing">15. Suggested release sequencing</h2> <ol type="1"> <li>Harden and gate (P0 security, accessibility, and continuous integration items). These protect users and unblock everything else. This is the 1.0 quality bar.</li> <li>Land the QUILL key flagship (QK-1 through QK-5, NAV-1, NAV-4, SEL-1 through SEL-3) plus the primer and first tutorials. This is the story that makes QUILL memorable.</li> <li>Decompose main_frame safely (CQ-16 then CQ-1) to make all future work faster and lower risk.</li> <li>Performance polish (PERF-1 through PERF-3 and PERF-9) so first use feels instant.</li> <li>Documentation and launch content (remaining podcasts and tutorials, keyboard reference, developer quickstart) so launch lands with a complete learning surface.</li> <li>Post-1.0 delight and expansion (P2 and P3) guided by beta feedback.</li> </ol> <p>Definition of greatness for this plan: when a first-time blind writer can open QUILL, discover the QUILL key, navigate a messy document by structure, fix it, read it back, and save it, all by keyboard, with every step confirmed clearly, and a returning power user can do the same in silence at speed, then QUILL is golden.</p> <hr /> <h2 id="part-ii-verified-line-by-line-audit-2026-06-01">Part II: Verified line-by-line audit (2026-06-01)</h2> <p>This part records a structured, tool-assisted audit that read across the entire source tree (148 Python files, 37,559 lines), all documentation, the test suite (118 test files), and the build and release scripts. Findings below are concrete and carry file-and-line citations so they can be acted on directly. Each new actionable item is added to the backlog in section 16.10 with a stable ID, and the P0 correctness bugs are also called out at the top because several are latent crashes.</p> <p>Tooling run for this audit:</p> <ul> <li>ruff on the <code>quill</code> package: 113 findings (83 line-too-long, 10 undefined-name, 7 unsorted-imports, 5 unused-import, 3 quoted-annotation, 2 zip-without-strict, 2 unused-variable, 1 redefinition). On <code>tests</code> and <code>scripts</code>: 36 findings.</li> <li>mypy scoped to <code>quill/core</code> and <code>quill/io</code> (the strict zone): 44 errors across 14 files. Important correction to earlier notes: the strict zone is not currently clean; only the two AI files touched in a previous session were verified green. The scoped command remains <code>mypy quill\core quill\io</code> to avoid the whole-tree scan that previously exhausted memory.</li> </ul> <h3 id="161-confirmed-correctness-bugs-latent-crashes-highest-priority">16.1 Confirmed correctness bugs (latent crashes), highest priority</h3> <p>These are real defects found by reading the code, several confirmed by ruff undefined-name analysis. They should be fixed before 1.0.</p> <ol type="1"> <li>Corrupted method <code>_show_bw_onboarding</code> in <a href="../../quill/ui/main_frame.py#L19426">quill/ui/main_frame.py</a> (lines 19426 to 19470). The method body contains copy-pasted "Insert Link" dialog code and references undefined names <code>selected_text</code> (line 19442), <code>dialog</code> (line 19463), and <code>profiles</code> (line 19470), plus assigns <code>display_text</code> and <code>url</code> that are never used. If this onboarding path is reached it raises <code>NameError</code>. The intended behavior is to confirm the BITS Whisperer rollout and then present a profile choice. This is a P0 crash. See BUG-1.</li> <li>Four bare <code>wx.</code> calls that should be <code>self._wx.</code> in <a href="../../quill/ui/main_frame.py#L16983">quill/ui/main_frame.py</a> at lines 16983, 17015, 17022, and 17042 (<code>wx.GetSingleChoice</code> and <code>wx.GetTextFromUser</code> in the heading-style prompts). Module-level <code>wx</code> is not imported; it is only stored as <code>self._wx</code> (assigned around line 683). These four call sites raise <code>NameError</code> at runtime when the heading-style flow executes. This is a P0 crash on a real user path. See BUG-2.</li> <li>Undefined type annotation <code>VoiceOption</code> in <a href="../../quill/ui/main_frame.py#L12503">quill/ui/main_frame.py</a> at lines 12503 and 12532. The symbol is imported as <code>ReadAloudVoiceOption</code> (around line 240) but the annotations use the bare name. With <code>from __future__ import annotations</code> this does not crash at call time, but it breaks <code>typing.get_type_hints</code> and static analysis. Fix by using the imported alias. See BUG-3.</li> <li>Redefinition of <code>URLError</code> in <a href="../../quill/ui/main_frame.py#L339">quill/ui/main_frame.py</a>: imported first from <code>urllib.error</code> (line 15) and again from <code>quill.core.updates</code> (line 339). The second import shadows the first. Pick one source. See BUG-4.</li> <li>Unchecked llama.cpp response shape in <a href="../../quill/core/ai/llama_cpp_backend.py#L113">quill/core/ai/llama_cpp_backend.py</a> (lines 113 to 117): <code>out["choices"][0]["message"]["content"]</code> will raise <code>KeyError</code> or <code>IndexError</code> on a malformed or version-mismatched response. Add validation and a friendly error. See BUG-5.</li> <li>XML element handling bug in <a href="../../quill/io/structured.py#L614">quill/io/structured.py</a> (lines 614 and 615): a <code>list[str]</code> is assigned where an <code>Element</code> is expected and then passed to <code>str.join</code>, which mypy flags as an assignment and arg-type error. This is a real type-level defect in the DOCX path. See BUG-6.</li> <li>Potential infinite loop in <a href="../../quill/core/ai/assistant.py#L196">quill/core/ai/assistant.py</a> chunk splitting if <code>max_chars <= 0</code> is ever passed; add a guard. See BUG-7.</li> </ol> <h3 id="162-security-findings-verified">16.2 Security findings (verified)</h3> <p>Highest priority first. Most user files live under the trusted per-user app data directory, so the focus is tampered configuration, untrusted document inputs, and supply chain.</p> <ol type="1"> <li>XML entity expansion (billion laughs) in document parsing. <a href="../../quill/io/structured.py#L416">quill/io/structured.py</a> uses <code>ET.fromstring</code> for XML (line 416), DOCX <code>word/document.xml</code> (around line 408), and PPTX slide XML; <a href="../../quill/io/pages.py#L107">quill/io/pages.py</a> parses PPTX XML similarly. None disable entity expansion, so a crafted file can cause memory and CPU exhaustion. Fix by switching to <code>defusedxml</code> or a hardened parser for all untrusted XML. P0 hardening. See SEC-10.</li> <li>Decompression bombs in ZIP-based formats (DOCX, XLSX, ODT, PPTX) in <a href="../../quill/io/structured.py#L604">quill/io/structured.py</a> (around lines 604, 683, 717). The archives are read without checking total uncompressed size. Add a cumulative size limit before reading entries. See SEC-11.</li> <li>Subprocess executable paths sourced from settings. <a href="../../quill/core/external_tools.py#L132">quill/core/external_tools.py</a> (around line 132) expands and runs configured executable paths (for example the DECtalk executable and other engines) without validating they live in a trusted location. If <code>settings.json</code> is tampered, this is arbitrary code execution. Validate against an allowlist or bundled or <code>shutil.which</code>-resolved path. This pairs with the earlier SEC-1. See SEC-1.</li> <li>PATH hijacking via tool discovery in <a href="../../quill/core/external_tools.py#L102">quill/core/external_tools.py</a> (around lines 102 to 115): <code>shutil.which</code> trusts the process PATH. Document the risk and prefer bundled tool paths where available. See SEC-12.</li> <li>Update download without binary checksum or signature verification in <a href="../../quill/core/updates.py#L249">quill/core/updates.py</a> (around line 249). The manifest signature is verified, but the downloaded asset itself is not checksum-verified before use. Verify a hash from the signed manifest against the downloaded bytes. This pairs with SEC-6. See SEC-6.</li> <li>Incomplete secret redaction in diagnostics. <a href="../../quill/core/diagnostics.py#L20">quill/core/diagnostics.py</a> (around lines 20 to 29) redacts <code>Authorization: Bearer</code> style tokens but misses patterns like <code>token:</code>, <code>password:</code>, and <code>NAME_KEY=</code> environment assignments. Broaden the redaction patterns so diagnostic bundles never leak partial secrets. See SEC-13.</li> <li>Python sandbox environment and resource limits. <a href="../../quill/core/python_sandbox.py#L143">quill/core/python_sandbox.py</a> inherits <code>PATH</code> into the subprocess (around line 143) and passes the user code as a base64 environment variable (around line 145), which can appear in a process list on shared systems; there is also no wall-clock or memory cap beyond the timeout. Add memory and CPU limits and avoid leaking the payload via the environment where possible. This refines SEC-9. See SEC-9, SEC-14.</li> <li><code>run_subprocess_safely</code> does not validate <code>cwd</code> or the executable in <a href="../../quill/stability/safe_subprocess.py#L11">quill/stability/safe_subprocess.py</a> (around lines 11 to 26), and only catches <code>TimeoutExpired</code>, not <code>OSError</code> or <code>FileNotFoundError</code>. Add validation and wrap the missing exception. This refines SEC-4. See SEC-4, SEC-15.</li> <li>Credential and Keychain input validation. <a href="../../quill/platform/windows/credential_manager.py#L73">quill/platform/windows/credential_manager.py</a> does not validate <code>target_name</code> (around lines 73 to 99), and <a href="../../quill/platform/macos/keychain.py#L30">quill/platform/macos/keychain.py</a> does not check the <code>security</code> subprocess return code in <code>set_secret</code> (around lines 30 to 50). Validate names against a safe pattern and check return codes. See SEC-16.</li> <li>Shell integration registry command in <a href="../../quill/platform/windows/shell_integration.py#L35">quill/platform/windows/shell_integration.py</a> is safe today because it derives from <code>launcher_command()</code>, but it is not escaped; document that it must never accept user input, or escape it if that changes. See SEC-17.</li> </ol> <h3 id="163-correctness-and-robustness-non-crashing-findings">16.3 Correctness and robustness (non-crashing) findings</h3> <ol type="1"> <li>Windows atomic write is not guaranteed. <a href="../../quill/core/storage.py#L16">quill/core/storage.py</a> uses temp file plus <code>replace</code> (around line 16). On Windows this can be a two-step operation under contention. Confirm <code>os.replace</code> semantics and, where needed, add retry-on-<code>PermissionError</code> so a concurrent reader cannot cause data loss. See CQ-19.</li> <li>Version comparison ignores pre-release suffixes in <a href="../../quill/core/updates.py#L136">quill/core/updates.py</a> (around line 136): <code>1.2.0-rc1</code> parses as <code>1.2.0</code>, so a release candidate sorts equal to the stable. Decide and document the intended ordering. See CQ-20.</li> <li>Snippet placeholder regex does not handle nested braces in <a href="../../quill/core/snippets.py#L90">quill/core/snippets.py</a> (around lines 90 to 120). Document the limitation or support nesting. See FEAT-5.</li> <li>TOML parse has no guard in <a href="../../quill/core/compliance.py#L142">quill/core/compliance.py</a> (around lines 142 to 160): a corrupted <code>pyproject.toml</code> aborts the dependency audit. Wrap and report. See CQ-21.</li> <li>Credential empty-blob path in <a href="../../quill/platform/windows/credential_manager.py#L68">quill/platform/windows/credential_manager.py</a> returns an empty secret indistinguishable from absent; log and document. See CQ-22.</li> </ol> <h3 id="164-typing-gaps-in-the-strict-zone-the-44-mypy-errors">16.4 Typing gaps in the strict zone (the 44 mypy errors)</h3> <p>The strict zone (<code>quill/core</code> and <code>quill/io</code>) currently reports 44 errors in 14 files. Representative clusters, all to be driven to zero and then kept green in continuous integration (see CQ-7):</p> <ul> <li><a href="../../quill/core/ipc.py#L75">quill/core/ipc.py</a>: six errors from a <code>handle: object</code> annotation that is then used as a file object, plus <code>fcntl</code> attributes that are POSIX-only. The cross-platform branch on <code>os.name</code> is logically sound; annotate the handle as <code>IO[bytes]</code> or <code>Any</code> and guard the <code>fcntl</code> import for type-checkers. See TYPE-1.</li> <li><a href="../../quill/core/bw_speech.py#L169">quill/core/bw_speech.py</a>: an <code>Any</code> returned where <code>float</code> is declared (line 169), missing parameter annotations (lines 223, 255), and the optional <code>faster_whisper</code> import. See TYPE-2.</li> <li><a href="../../quill/core/read_aloud.py#L298">quill/core/read_aloud.py</a>: the <code>kokoro.KPipeline</code> attribute is not visible to mypy (line 298); fix the ignore code. See TYPE-3.</li> <li><a href="../../quill/core/dictation.py#L10">quill/core/dictation.py</a>: <code>None</code> assigned to a <code>Callable</code>-typed name (line 10), and <code>recognize_whisper</code> and <code>recognize_vosk</code> on an untyped recognizer (lines 71, 78). See TYPE-4.</li> <li><a href="../../quill/io/pages.py#L73">quill/io/pages.py</a>: missing return and parameter annotations (lines 73, 78, 91), untyped third-party <code>keynote_parser</code>, and an <code>Any</code> returned as <code>str</code> (line 238). See TYPE-5.</li> <li><a href="../../quill/io/structured.py#L173">quill/io/structured.py</a>: untyped <code>openpyxl</code> import (line 173), a missing annotation (line 249), and the Element bug from 16.1 item 6 (lines 614, 615). See TYPE-6, BUG-6.</li> <li><a href="../../quill/core/ai/llama_cpp_backend.py#L65">quill/core/ai/llama_cpp_backend.py</a>: missing annotations (lines 65, 71), a <code>None</code>-typed attribute later assigned a <code>Llama</code> (line 82), and an <code>Any</code> returned as <code>str</code> (line 118). See TYPE-7.</li> <li><a href="../../quill/core/ai/assistant.py#L130">quill/core/ai/assistant.py</a>: missing annotations (lines 130, 200). See TYPE-8.</li> </ul> <p>Where third-party stubs are missing (<code>openpyxl</code>, <code>faster_whisper</code>, <code>keynote_parser</code>, <code>kokoro</code>, <code>llama_cpp</code>), either install the available stub packages (for example <code>types-openpyxl</code>) or add precise per-import ignores with the correct error codes, and add Protocols for the SDK handles so the strict zone stays honest.</p> <h3 id="165-performance-findings-verified">16.5 Performance findings (verified)</h3> <ol type="1"> <li>Spell-check wordlist loads synchronously (about 370,000 words) in <a href="../../quill/core/spellcheck.py#L100">quill/core/spellcheck.py</a> (around lines 100 to 115), under the backend lock, stalling the first check. Background preload at startup. Pairs with PERF-1. See PERF-1.</li> <li>Thesaurus index loads synchronously (a large data file) in <a href="../../quill/core/thesaurus.py#L52">quill/core/thesaurus.py</a> (around lines 52 to 60) on first lookup. Background preload. Pairs with PERF-2. See PERF-2.</li> <li>Read Aloud accumulates uncompressed audio arrays in memory in <a href="../../quill/core/read_aloud.py#L295">quill/core/read_aloud.py</a> (around lines 295 to 325); stream to file for long documents, and cache identical sentences. Pairs with PERF-3. See PERF-3, PERF-10.</li> <li>Spreadsheet reading loads entire worksheets into memory in <a href="../../quill/io/structured.py#L193">quill/io/structured.py</a> (around lines 193 to 199); cap rows or stream. See PERF-11.</li> <li>DOCX and PPTX load whole XML payloads and build full in-memory documents in <a href="../../quill/io/structured.py#L604">quill/io/structured.py</a> (around lines 604 and 637); consider streaming and run these off the UI thread. See PERF-12.</li> <li>PDF extraction materializes all pages in <a href="../../quill/io/pdf.py#L58">quill/io/pdf.py</a> (around line 58); page-stream for very large PDFs. See PERF-13.</li> <li>File search scans whole documents with no chunking in <a href="../../quill/core/file_search.py#L48">quill/core/file_search.py</a> (around lines 48 to 70); stream large corpora. See PERF-14.</li> </ol> <p>Concurrency note (correction): the spell-check wordlist cache, the enchant dictionary, the thesaurus index, and the watch-folder seen-set all already use <code>threading.Lock</code>. There is no missing lock there. The remaining work is documenting these invariants (CQ-17) and the Windows atomic-write behavior (CQ-19).</p> <h3 id="166-main_framepy-decomposition-map-verified-seams">16.6 main_frame.py decomposition map (verified seams)</h3> <p>The 18,748-line <a href="../../quill/ui/main_frame.py">quill/ui/main_frame.py</a> divides cleanly into roughly 22 subsystems. This map is the basis for CQ-1 (extract behind characterization tests, CQ-16):</p> <ul> <li>Initialization and setup: lines 678 to 860.</li> <li>Command registry and keybinding: lines 971 to 4975.</li> <li>Menu building and identifier management: lines 2358 to 4640 (the single largest block).</li> <li>Event binding and frame lifecycle: lines 4927 to 6663.</li> <li>QUILL key mode: lines 5162 to 5287.</li> <li>Browse and navigation (Quick Nav, ARIA regions): lines 5358 to 5817.</li> <li>Tab and document management: lines 5016 to 5120 and 5781 to 5860.</li> <li>Text editor operations: lines 5849 to 6201.</li> <li>Context menus: lines 6206 to 6650.</li> <li>Status bar: lines 7252 to 7675.</li> <li>Dialogs and modal presentation: lines 7675 to 7702.</li> <li>File input/output and sessions: lines 7067 to 7141 and 8075 to 8824.</li> <li>Speech and Read Aloud: lines 12400 to 13460.</li> <li>Update checking: lines 14963 to 15100.</li> <li>Find and replace: lines 15655 to 16000.</li> <li>Link insertion: lines 16080 to 16210.</li> <li>Heading styles: lines 16950 to 17060 (contains BUG-2).</li> <li>List manager: lines 17259 to 17700.</li> <li>Intellisense and autocomplete: lines 18079 to 18240.</li> <li>Onboarding and first run: lines 14369 to 19700 (contains BUG-1).</li> </ul> <h3 id="167-io-contract-and-coverage-findings">16.7 IO contract and coverage findings</h3> <ul> <li>Readers that follow <code>read(path) -> Document</code> and raise on error are compliant (text and structured confirmed). Several formats are read-only by design (PDF, Pages) and lack <code>write</code>; only Pages implements <code>outline</code>. If the product promises <code>outline</code> for structured formats, add it for DOCX, PPTX, and XLSX. See IO-1.</li> <li>Format test coverage is thin: only text, PDF, OCR, pandoc, and structured have any tests, and pandoc and structured are minimal. There are no fixtures exercising real conversions. The "100-plus formats" claim rests almost entirely on pandoc and is essentially untested end to end. See CQ-13 and the test plan in 16.9.</li> </ul> <h3 id="168-documentation-findings-verified">16.8 Documentation findings (verified)</h3> <ul> <li>Missing entirely: API or module reference, developer quickstart, plugin developer guide, a static (offline) keyboard reference, a configuration schema reference, a troubleshooting guide, and any podcast transcripts or tutorial or video scripts. See DOC-1 through DOC-6, DOC-7, DOC-8, and the POD and TUT items.</li> <li>The accessibility conformance report at <a href="../accessibility/acr-vpat.md">docs/accessibility/acr-vpat.md</a> is a template with placeholder evidence. It must be either filled in with a real 0.1.5 assessment or clearly labeled as not yet assessed. See DOC-9.</li> <li>The PRD at <a href="../QUILL-PRD.md">docs/QUILL-PRD.md</a> mixes 1.0 specification with 0.1.5 reality; its header should state plainly that it specifies 1.0 and that 0.1.5 implements the subset marked in the roadmap mapping. See DOC-10.</li> <li>Documentation accessibility: the PRD uses emoji (check marks, warning and cross symbols, and others) and em-dashes throughout. Per the project's own markdown accessibility rules, replace emoji with text labels such as the words pass, warning, and error, and replace em-dashes. This applies to the source markdown so the generated HTML and EPUB inherit the fix. See DOC-11.</li> <li>The engineering docs (architecture, module-contracts, data-layout, runtime-model, diagnostics-runbook, quality-gates) are useful but skeletal (most under 50 lines). Expand them alongside the API reference. See DOC-12.</li> <li>User guide gaps: concrete AI setup examples (for example connecting to a local Ollama endpoint and an error matrix for 401 versus 403 versus 500), spell-check dictionary workflow, watch-folder walkthrough, and a troubleshooting section (Quick Nav key conflicts, garbled PDF extraction, autosave disk pressure). See DOC-13.</li> </ul> <h3 id="169-test-strategy-findings-verified">16.9 Test strategy findings (verified)</h3> <ul> <li>Inventory: 118 test files. Core has the most coverage; the UI monolith, the IO format matrix, integration, performance, and accessibility content depth are the weak spots.</li> <li>The 18,748-line UI has only a handful of behavior tests. Before decomposition (CQ-1), add a characterization suite (CQ-16) covering tab lifecycle, undo and redo isolation, autosave and recovery, session restore, Quick Nav, find and replace, spell-check as you type, sticky notes, and macros.</li> <li>Add policy and attack-surface tests for the Python sandbox (allowed versus blocked modules, escape attempts, resource limits), spell-check tier fallback, Read Aloud backend fallback, and IO format smoke tests with real fixtures. See CQ-11, CQ-13, CQ-23, CQ-24.</li> <li>Performance tests are smoke-level only; add the budget suite (PERF-9).</li> <li>Scripts: the release orchestrator <a href="../../scripts/release_readiness.py">scripts/release_readiness.py</a> runs ruff, pip-audit strict, pytest, docs build, and corpus verification, but there is no dependency lockfile and no timeouts on long commands; the Windows build pins an embeddable Python by a hardcoded hash that requires a code change to rotate. See CQ-25, CQ-26.</li> </ul> <h3 id="1610-new-backlog-items-from-the-verified-audit">16.10 New backlog items from the verified audit</h3> <p>These extend the section 14 tracker. The bootstrap applies resource limits before running user code: on Windows a Job Object caps process memory (<code>JOBOBJECT_EXTENDED_LIMIT_INFORMATION</code> with <code>JOB_OBJECT_LIMIT_PROCESS_MEMORY</code>, kernel32 functions declared with explicit <code>restype</code>/<code>argtypes</code> so the 64-bit HANDLE is not truncated); on POSIX <code>setrlimit</code> caps <code>RLIMIT_AS</code> and <code>RLIMIT_CPU</code>. A new <code>memory_limit_mb</code> parameter (default 512) and a CPU budget of <code>timeout + 1s</code> are passed in the payload. Tests (6) in <code>tests/unit/core/test_python_sandbox.py</code> assert the payload is delivered via stdin (never <code>QUILL_SANDBOX_PAYLOAD</code> in env), the payload carries the resource limits, and — on Windows — a 64 MB cap actually fails a ~60 M-int allocation.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>SEC-15</td> <td>safe_subprocess validates cwd and wraps OSError</td> <td>Security</td> <td>S</td> <td>Done</td> <td><code>cwd</code> and executable are validated; <code>OSError</code> and <code>FileNotFoundError</code> are caught and surfaced clearly; test included. The executable is derived from <code>sys.executable</code> (never user-supplied), and <code>action</code> is validated against the closed <code>verb_actions()</code> registry — an unknown action raises <code>ValueError</code> rather than reaching the registry. <td>M</td> <td>Done</td> <td>Long-document synthesis stays flat in memory and reuses identical sentences. Read Aloud already renders one sentence at a time to a temporary WAV and deletes it (<code>_run_wav_sentences</code>), so audio is never materialized for the whole document; the new <code>quill/core/tts_cache.py</code> LRU (PERF-3) adds bounded, disk-backed caching of identical sentences with both an entry-count and a byte budget so the cache itself cannot spike memory or disk. Benchmark <code>tests/performance/test_tts_cache_benchmark.py::test_long_document_only_renders_unique_sentences</code> confirms a 100-sentence document built from 5 unique lines synthesizes only 5 times, and <code>test_byte_budget_bounds_total_size</code> confirms the bound holds.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>PERF-11</td> <td>Cap or stream spreadsheet reads</td> <td>Performance</td> <td>S</td> <td>Done</td> <td>Large sheets do not exhaust memory; a row cap or streaming applies. openpyxl reads run in <code>read_only=True</code> streaming mode and <code>quill/io/structured.py</code> stops at <code>_SPREADSHEET_MAX_ROWS</code> (50) and <code>_SPREADSHEET_MAX_COLS</code> (20) so an extract never materializes an unbounded sheet; covered by <code>tests/unit/io/test_open_read.py</code> and source-contract tests in <code>tests/unit/ui/test_main_frame_open_threading.py</code>.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>PERF-13</td> <td>Page-stream large PDFs</td> <td>Performance</td> <td>S</td> <td>Done</td> <td>Very large PDFs extract without materializing all pages at once. <code>quill/io/pdf.py</code> iterates <code>pdf.pages</code>/<code>reader.pages</code> lazily (no <code>list(pdf.pages)</code>), flushes pdfplumber's per-page cache as it goes, and stops at <code>_PDF_MAX_PAGES</code> (200) so a huge PDF cannot pull text from every page at once while still reporting the full <code>page_count</code>; covered by <code>tests/unit/io/test_pdf.py::test_pypdf_extraction_caps_pages_so_a_huge_pdf_cannot_materialize_every_page</code> (100k-page stub extracts only the cap).</td> </tr> <tr> <td>PERF-14</td> <td>Chunk file search over large corpora</td> <td>Performance</td> <td>S</td> <td>Done</td> <td>Search streams large inputs without quadratic blowups. <code>quill/core/file_search.py</code> now groups matches to lines with a precomputed line-start table and a <code>bisect_right</code> lookup, so mapping M matches over L lines is O(M log L) instead of the previous O(M * L) per-match linear scan; covered by <code>tests/unit/core/test_file_search.py::test_search_groups_many_matches_to_correct_lines_without_quadratic_scan</code> (5000 matches map to correct lines).</td> </tr> <tr> <td>IO-1</td> <td>Add outline support for structured formats</td> <td>IO</td> <td>M</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>DOCX, PPTX, and XLSX provide an outline, or the contract is amended and documented.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>DOC-7</td> <td>Configuration schema reference</td> <td>Docs</td> <td>M</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>Settings, keymap, and data schemas are documented for pre-configuration.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>DOC-8</td> <td>Troubleshooting guide</td> <td>Docs</td> <td>S</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>Common issues (key conflicts, PDF extraction, AI connection, autosave) are documented with fixes.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>DOC-9</td> <td>Replace or label the ACR template</td> <td>Docs</td> <td>M</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>The conformance report reflects a real 0.1.5 assessment or is clearly marked not yet assessed.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>DOC-10</td> <td>Clarify 1.0 versus 0.1.5 in the PRD header</td> <td>Docs</td> <td>S</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>The PRD states its 1.0 scope and the 0.1.5 implemented subset.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>DOC-11</td> <td>Make the PRD and docs accessible</td> <td>Docs</td> <td>M</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>Emoji are replaced with text labels and em-dashes removed across docs source; artifacts regenerated and the docs gate passes.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>DOC-12</td> <td>Expand engineering docs</td> <td>Docs</td> <td>M</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>Architecture, contracts, data layout, runtime model, diagnostics, and quality gates are filled out beyond stubs.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>DOC-13</td> <td>Fill user-guide gaps</td> <td>Docs</td> <td>M</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>AI setup examples, spell-check dictionary workflow, watch-folder walkthrough, and troubleshooting are added.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <h3 id="1611-summary-of-verified-counts">16.11 Summary of verified counts</h3> <ul> <li>Confirmed latent-crash bugs: 7 (BUG-1 through BUG-7), of which two (BUG-1, BUG-2) are on real user paths in the UI.</li> <li>Security findings: 10 verified items spanning untrusted-input parsing, supply chain, secret handling, and subprocess and credential validation.</li> <li>Strict-zone typing errors: 44 across 14 files (TYPE-1 through TYPE-8 cover the clusters).</li> <li>Lint findings: 113 in the package and 36 in tests and scripts (CQ-18).</li> <li>Performance hotspots: 7 verified (PERF-1, PERF-2, PERF-3, PERF-10 through PERF-14).</li> <li>Documentation gaps: 7 missing artifacts plus accessibility and version-clarity fixes (DOC-1 through DOC-13).</li> <li>Test gaps: the UI monolith, the IO format matrix, sandbox policy, and a performance budget are the highest-value additions.</li> </ul> <p>Revised sequencing note: the new P0 correctness bugs (BUG-1 and BUG-2 especially) and the untrusted-input hardening (SEC-10, SEC-11) should be folded into step 1 of the section 15 sequencing, because they are small, concrete, and protect users immediately.</p> <hr /> <h2 id="part-iii-quality-gates-and-the-ai-and-agent-program">Part III: Quality gates and the AI and agent program</h2> <p>This part does two bold things. First, it defines a ladder of automated quality gates so that every change (whether written by a person or by an AI coding assistant such as Copilot) is held to a high, consistent, machine-checked bar before it can merge. Second, it reimagines QUILL's own AI and agent features so they become a signature strength: local-first, fully accessible, consented, reversible, and genuinely useful to a blind or low-vision writer.</p> <p>The two are connected. Strong gates are what let a team move fast with AI assistance without drifting in quality. They turn "the AI wrote it" from a risk into an advantage, because nothing reaches users that has not passed the same objective checks.</p> <h3 id="17-quality-gates-for-an-ai-assisted-workflow">17. Quality gates for an AI-assisted workflow</h3> <p>The repository already has the raw materials: ruff, mypy, pytest, a docs-artifact gate, pip-audit in the release script, accessibility and performance test folders, and a release readiness orchestrator. The work is to assemble these into an explicit, enforced gate ladder, close the holes the audit found, and make the gates fast enough to run on every change.</p> <h4 id="171-the-gate-ladder">17.1 The gate ladder</h4> <p>Three tiers, each stricter than the last:</p> <ul> <li>Pre-commit (local, seconds). Format and lint the changed files, run quick syntax and undefined-name checks, and block commits that fail. This catches the class of bug the audit found (bare <code>wx.</code> calls, undefined names, unsorted imports) before they ever leave a developer's machine. See GATE-1.</li> <li>Pull request (continuous integration, minutes). The full objective bar that must be green to merge: lint, scoped strict typing, the test suite with a coverage floor, the accessibility checks, the docs-artifact gate, and the security scans. See GATE-2 through GATE-9.</li> <li>Release (pre-tag, thorough). The existing release readiness orchestrator, hardened: pinned dependencies, command timeouts, corpus verification, performance budgets, and provenance and software bill of materials generation. See GATE-10, CQ-25, CQ-26.</li> </ul> <h4 id="172-the-specific-gates-to-enforce">17.2 The specific gates to enforce</h4> <ul> <li>Lint gate. Ruff must be clean (or explicitly justified) on the package, tests, and scripts. Closes the 113 plus 36 findings and keeps them closed. See GATE-2, CQ-18.</li> <li>Typing gate. Strict mypy on <code>quill/core</code> and <code>quill/io</code>, always scoped to those paths (never the whole tree, which previously froze a machine), must report zero errors. Drives the 44 strict-zone errors to zero and holds the line. See GATE-3, CQ-7.</li> <li>Banned-pattern gate. A small, fast check that fails the build on known footguns: a bare <code>wx.</code> reference in <code>main_frame</code> (must be <code>self._wx</code>), undefined names, duplicate imports, <code>print</code> left in library code, <code>ET.fromstring</code> on untrusted XML (must use the hardened parser), and <code>except Exception</code> without a logged cause. This is the gate that would have caught BUG-1, BUG-2, BUG-4, and SEC-10 automatically. See GATE-4.</li> <li>Test and coverage gate. The full pytest suite (unit, integration, accessibility, performance smoke) must pass, with a coverage floor that ratchets upward over time and a hard floor for <code>quill/core</code> and <code>quill/io</code>. New code may not lower coverage. See GATE-5, CQ-13.</li> <li>Characterization gate for the UI monolith. Before and during the <code>main_frame</code> decomposition, a characterization suite must pass so refactors are provably behavior-preserving. See GATE-6, CQ-16, CQ-1.</li> <li>Accessibility gate. Keyboard-trap and contrast checks, plus the announcement-grammar and focus-order assertions, run on every pull request, not on demand. No UI change merges if it regresses screen-reader operability. See GATE-7, A11Y items.</li> <li>Security gate. pip-audit (strict) for dependency vulnerabilities, a static security scan (for example bandit or semgrep) for subprocess, XML, and path-traversal patterns, a check that all untrusted XML uses the hardened parser, and a "no plaintext secret" scan of diagnostics output. See GATE-8, SEC-10 through SEC-17.</li> <li>No-silent-network gate. An automated test asserts that no AI or network code path makes an outbound call without explicit consent, and that provider, model, and scope are always surfaced. This makes the product's core trust promise machine-enforced, not just a convention. See GATE-9, AI-5.</li> <li>Docs-artifact and accessibility gate. Every changed Markdown file regenerates its HTML and EPUB, and the docs accessibility rules (no emoji, no em-dashes, accessible tables, meaningful links) are linted. See GATE-2 (docs job), DOC-11, DOC-5.</li> <li>Performance budget gate. Startup time, first spell-check, first thesaurus lookup, large-document Quick Nav, and Read Aloud start must stay within published budgets; a regression fails the build. See GATE-10, PERF-9.</li> <li>Module-size budget gate. A soft, ratcheting budget on the largest files (starting with <code>main_frame</code>) that prevents new growth and rewards extraction, so the monolith shrinks monotonically. See GATE-11, CQ-1.</li> </ul> <h4 id="173-make-ai-coding-assistants-productive-and-safe-in-this-repo">17.3 Make AI coding assistants productive and safe in this repo</h4> <p>The goal is that an AI assistant (Copilot or an agent) can contribute high-quality, accessible, secure code with minimal back-and-forth, because the repository tells it exactly how, and the gates catch anything that slips.</p> <ul> <li>Strengthen the repository guidance. Expand the existing <code>.github/copilot-instructions.md</code> and add an <code>AGENTS.md</code> so any assistant has a crisp, current description of the architecture, the strict-typing zone, the scoped mypy command, the accessibility non-negotiables, the no-silent-network rule, the PowerShell and commit conventions, and the definition of done. See GATE-12.</li> <li>Ship a machine-readable definition of done. A short checklist (accessible, typed in the strict zone, tested, lint-clean, no silent network, docs regenerated) that both humans and agents follow, mirrored by the gates so the checklist is actually enforced. See GATE-13.</li> <li>Encode the footguns the audit found. Document the bare <code>wx.</code> versus <code>self._wx</code> rule, the hardened-XML rule, the scoped-mypy rule, and the path-safety helper directly in the guidance, with examples, so assistants do not reintroduce them. See GATE-12.</li> <li>Add CODEOWNERS and required reviews for the highest-risk areas (security, the sandbox, the AI provider boundary, the platform secret stores) so sensitive changes always get human eyes even when AI-authored. See GATE-14.</li> <li>Provide test-first scaffolding. Templates and fixtures (IO sample files, an accessibility test harness, a sandbox policy harness) so an assistant can write the test alongside the change and the coverage gate is easy to satisfy. See GATE-5, CQ-23, CQ-13.</li> <li>Keep the guidance honest over time. A periodic check that the instructions match reality (version, commands, structure), so assistants are never working from stale facts. See GATE-12.</li> </ul> <h3 id="18-make-quills-own-ai-and-agents-amazing">18. Make QUILL's own AI and agents amazing</h3> <p>QUILL already has a thoughtful AI layer: a provider and model boundary, an enable toggle with an honest status badge, an Assistant Hub, Ask QUILL chat, model and connection management, a Writing Assistant, a Prompt Studio, an Agent Center scaffold, selection actions, style training, and a Speech submenu, all gated behind explicit consent with no silent network calls. The bold move is to turn this solid foundation into the most accessible AI writing experience anywhere: local-first, fully spoken, always reversible, and genuinely agentic for the tasks that matter most to this audience.</p> <p>Guiding principles for all AI and agent work, non-negotiable:</p> <ul> <li>Local-first and private by default. On-device models (llama.cpp and Apple Foundation Models) are first-class; any cloud use is explicit, per-action, and clearly labeled. See AI-5.</li> <li>Consent, visibility, and reversibility. Every AI action shows provider, model, and scope, streams visible progress, and produces a result the user can review and undo. No AI edit is ever silent or irreversible. See AI-5, AI-7.</li> <li>Accessible to the core. Every AI surface is fully keyboard and screen-reader operable, with results that read well top to bottom and diffs that can be reviewed line by line by ear. See A11Y items.</li> </ul> <h4 id="181-make-the-assistant-feel-magical">18.1 Make the assistant feel magical</h4> <ul> <li>Streaming, announced responses. Replies stream incrementally with accessible, throttled announcements so the user hears progress without being flooded. See AI-1.</li> <li>Preview-and-apply diffs that are reviewable by ear. Any AI edit is presented as a structured, navigable diff (added, removed, changed), readable line by line with the screen reader, with apply, apply-partially, and reject, and a single undo. This is the feature that makes AI editing trustworthy for a blind writer. See AI-7.</li> <li>Context-aware actions. The actions offered adapt to the cursor or selection context (inside a list, a table, a heading, a code block) and to the document type, so the right help is always one key away, including from the QUILL key. See AI-8, HELP-1.</li> <li>A real prompt library. Save, name, organize, and share prompts and recipes, with a quick picker and live preview, building on Prompt Studio. See AI-9.</li> <li>Style that is truly yours. Strengthen style training so the assistant can match a user's voice, explain why it made a change, and stay consistent across a document. See AI-10.</li> </ul> <h4 id="182-a-genuine-accessible-agent-program">18.2 A genuine, accessible agent program</h4> <p>Move the Agent Center from scaffold to a small set of reliable, consented, reversible agents that each complete a real multi-step task and narrate every step. An agent never acts without consent, announces each step as it works, and produces a reviewable, undoable result.</p> <ul> <li>The Accessibility agent (the headline). Tell QUILL "make this document accessible" and it runs a consented, announced, reversible plan: audit structure, fix heading levels, add or improve alt text (with the user confirming each suggestion), tighten link text, apply plain-language improvements, then re-run the audit and report what changed. Every step is a reviewable diff and a single undo. This is the agent that embodies the product's mission. See AGENT-1.</li> <li>The Cleanup agent. Turn a messy imported document (bad OCR, broken structure, inconsistent formatting) into clean, well-structured text through a sequence of cleanup recipes, each announced and reversible. See AGENT-2, FEAT-8.</li> <li>The Review agent. Produce a spoken, skimmable review of a document (structure, readability, accessibility, consistency) with one-key jumps to each issue, building on the document health dashboard. See AGENT-3, FEAT-16.</li> <li>A safe, local agent loop. The agent runtime plans, takes one consented step at a time, can call only a small allowlist of in-app tools (navigate, edit-with-diff, run a sandboxed transform, run an audit), never the network without explicit consent, with a hard step cap and a guard against loops, and full step-by-step announcement. This reuses the existing sandbox and stability layers. See AGENT-4, SEC-9.</li> <li>Grounded answers over the user's own content. Optional, local retrieval over open documents and the sticky-notes vault so "ask QUILL" can answer from what the user is actually working on, always citing where an answer came from, never sending content anywhere without consent. See AI-11.</li> </ul> <h4 id="183-trust-safety-and-evaluation-for-ai">18.3 Trust, safety, and evaluation for AI</h4> <ul> <li>Machine-enforced no-silent-network, as a gate, not just a convention. See GATE-9, AI-5.</li> <li>An evaluation harness for AI quality. A small, repeatable set of tasks (accessibility fixes, cleanup, summarization) with expected-quality checks, so AI and agent changes can be measured and regressions caught before release. See AI-12.</li> <li>Redaction and offline integrity. Diagnostics never capture document content or secrets (SEC-13), and every AI feature degrades gracefully and announces clearly when a model is unavailable or a key is missing. See CQ-8, AI-6.</li> </ul> <h4 id="184-review-of-the-cloud-and-local-providers-openai-openrouter-gemini-azure-ollama-claude">18.4 Review of the cloud and local providers (OpenAI, OpenRouter, Gemini, Azure, Ollama, Claude)</h4> <p>A focused review of the provider boundary in <code>quill/core/assistant_ai.py</code>, the backends in <code>quill/core/ai/</code>, and how the UI wires them found one structural defect and several smaller correctness and enhancement gaps. The provider configuration surface is genuinely strong; the gap is that it is not yet connected to generation.</p> <ul> <li>The headline defect: configured providers never generate. <code>assistant_ai.py</code> fully implements provider selection, secure key storage (Credential Manager with a DPAPI fallback), HTTPS-only policy for cloud endpoints, model discovery, and connection verification for all six providers. But the <code>Assistant</code> is always constructed with no backend (<code>Assistant()</code> in <code>main_frame.py</code>), so generation always runs through <code>make_default_backend()</code>, which is Apple Foundation Models on macOS or local llama.cpp elsewhere. Selecting OpenAI, OpenRouter, Gemini, Azure OpenAI, Ollama, or Claude lets a user save a key, list models, and pass verification, yet every actual rewrite, summarize, chat, or agent step still runs on the local model. This is the single most important fix in the AI area: wire a provider-aware chat backend so the selected provider is the one that responds. See AI-13.</li> <li>Provider-specific correctness, needed once chat is wired: <ul> <li>OpenAI, OpenRouter, custom: standard <code>POST /v1/chat/completions</code>; OpenRouter benefits from optional <code>HTTP-Referer</code> and <code>X-Title</code> attribution headers.</li> <li>Claude: messages API at <code>POST /v1/messages</code> with <code>x-api-key</code>, <code>anthropic-version</code>, and a required <code>max_tokens</code>; the model-listing headers are already correct.</li> <li>Gemini: <code>POST /v1beta/models/{model}:generateContent</code> with <code>x-goog-api-key</code>; the request and response shape differ from the OpenAI schema and need their own adapter.</li> <li>Azure OpenAI: chat targets a deployment, not a model name, at <code>/openai/deployments/{deployment}/chat/completions?api-version=...</code>; the connection UI should make the deployment-versus-model distinction explicit. See AI-15.</li> <li>Ollama (local): generation should use <code>POST /api/chat</code>; model listing already uses <code>/api/tags</code> correctly.</li> </ul></li> <li>Streaming. No provider streams today; responses are blocking. Streaming with throttled, accessible announcements (AI-1) should be implemented once per provider in the shared backend so progress is heard, not awaited in silence. See AI-14.</li> <li>Tests and trust. There are no contract tests that exercise each provider's request and response shape. Add recorded or mocked per-provider contract tests (no live network in CI) so a provider change cannot silently break generation, and extend the existing, well-designed error taxonomy (auth, forbidden, rate-limited, warming-up, timeout) from the listing path to the chat path so users get the same cause-specific, screen-reader-friendly messages. See AI-16, AI-17.</li> <li>What is already good and should be preserved: the HTTPS-only policy with a careful local-loopback and private-network exception (a sound anti-SSRF posture), the Credential Manager plus DPAPI key handling with an honest "could not unlock on this device" status, the retry-with-backoff on transient categories, and the duplicate-tolerant model-name extraction across <code>models</code>, <code>data</code>, and <code>items</code> payload shapes.</li> </ul> <h4 id="185-on-the-github-copilot-sdk-a-measured-recommendation">18.5 On the GitHub Copilot SDK: a measured recommendation</h4> <p>The user is right to be cautious. The recommendation is to not ship or integrate the GitHub Copilot SDK as a flagship or default path for 1.0, and instead to treat it as an optional, clearly labeled provider behind the same AIBackend boundary, considered after 1.0. The reasoning:</p> <ul> <li>It would add real value: strong models, and for developer-leaning users a familiar, already-paid-for entitlement. That value is genuine and worth capturing eventually.</li> <li>But it conflicts with QUILL's core promises if made central. Copilot requires a paid subscription and an interactive GitHub OAuth device-flow sign-in, which is friction at odds with the local-first, bring-your-own-key, no-silent-network design and with the screen-reader-first simplicity of the connection flow. Its terms and telemetry posture are also a poorer fit for a privacy-first writing tool than a user's own API key.</li> <li>The pragmatic path: because the provider boundary is OpenAI-compatible, most of Copilot's value is already reachable through the existing custom OpenAI-compatible provider and through OpenAI, Claude, Gemini, and OpenRouter directly. So the marginal benefit of a dedicated Copilot integration is modest, while the cost (a bespoke auth flow, subscription gating, accessibility review of the sign-in, and ongoing terms compliance) is real. Add it later, gated and optional, only if beta users ask for it, and never as a default. See AI-18.</li> </ul> <h4 id="186-new-backlog-items-for-gates-and-ai">18.6 New backlog items for gates and AI</h4> <p>These extend the section 14 tracker.</p> <h5 id="quality-gates-mostly-p0-and-p1">Quality gates (mostly P0 and P1)</h5> <table> <thead> <tr> <th>ID</th> <th>Item</th> <th>Area</th> <th>Size</th> <th>Status</th> <th>Acceptance criteria</th> </tr> </thead> <tbody> <tr> <td>GATE-1</td> <td>Pre-commit hooks for format, lint, and quick checks</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>S</td> <td>Done</td> <td><code>.pre-commit-config.yaml</code> runs <code>ruff format</code> and <code>ruff check</code> (which includes the F821 undefined-name rule) on changed files, blocking failing commits locally; CONTRIBUTING documents one-time install.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>GATE-2</td> <td>Pull-request CI pipeline</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>M</td> <td>Done</td> <td><code>.github/workflows/pr-ci.yml</code> runs lint (<code>ruff format --check</code> and <code>ruff check</code> with E501 deferred to CQ-18), the full unit and accessibility suites with the coverage floor (GATE-5), and the MainFrame characterization snapshot (GATE-6). Together with Security CI (scoped typing GATE-3, banned patterns GATE-4, no-silent-network GATE-9, security checks GATE-8) and Accessibility CI (the a11y suite, docs-artifact diff, and dialog regressions), every required job runs on push and pull_request. Branch protection should require these checks before merge.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>GATE-3</td> <td>Strict typing gate (scoped)</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>S</td> <td>Done</td> <td><code>mypy quill\core quill\io</code> reports zero errors and is enforced by the <code>scoped-strict-typing</code> CI job (required for merge); third-party stub gaps are handled via <code>ignore_missing_imports</code> module overrides in pyproject; the whole-tree scan is never used.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>GATE-4</td> <td>Banned-pattern gate</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>S</td> <td>Done</td> <td><code>quill/tools/check_banned_patterns.py</code> (AST-based) fails on bare <code>wx.</code> in main_frame where <code>wx</code> is not locally bound (the BUG-2 class), on raw <code>ET.fromstring</code>/<code>etree.fromstring</code> outside <code>safe_xml</code> (the SEC-10 class), and on any removal of ruff's <code>F</code> rule group that enforces undefined-name (F821) and redefinition (F811) checks (the BUG-1/BUG-4 classes); a CI job runs it and tests cover the checker. The <code>except Exception</code> logged-cause sub-rule is tracked under CQ (it needs handler-body refactors across 26 sites) and is not claimed here.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>GATE-5</td> <td>Test and coverage floor</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>M</td> <td>Done</td> <td>The <code>unit-tests</code> job in <code>pr-ci.yml</code> runs the full <code>tests/unit</code> and <code>tests/accessibility</code> suites and enforces <code>--cov-fail-under=70</code> on <code>quill.core</code> and <code>quill.io</code> (current total 72.28%). <code>pytest-cov</code> is in the dev extras. The floor is a hard gate that must rise, never fall, as coverage improves; raising it is the mechanism for ratcheting.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>GATE-6</td> <td>Characterization gate for main_frame</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>M</td> <td>Done</td> <td><code>quill/tools/ui_surface.py</code> extracts the public method surface of <code>MainFrame</code> via AST (no <code>wx</code> needed) and a committed snapshot fixture (<code>tests/unit/ui/fixtures/main_frame_public_surface.json</code>, 235 methods) is checked by <code>tests/unit/ui/test_main_frame_characterization.py</code>, run as the <code>characterization</code> CI job. Any add/remove/rename of a public method fails until the snapshot is regenerated deliberately with <code>python -m quill.tools.ui_surface --write</code>, keeping the planned decomposition behavior-preserving.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>GATE-7</td> <td>Accessibility gate on every PR</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>M</td> <td>Done</td> <td>Accessibility CI runs on every pull request: the keyboard-trap and focus-order checks (<code>RegionTracker</code> in <code>tests/unit/core/test_a11y_regions.py</code>), the screen-reader announcement transcript suite (<code>tests/accessibility</code>), the dialog escape/default contract regressions, and the new announcement-grammar conformance suite (<code>tests/accessibility/test_announcement_grammar.py</code>) that asserts the A11Y-1 grammar stays well-formed. Contrast handling is covered by the high-contrast platform tests.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>GATE-8</td> <td>Security scan gate</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>M</td> <td>Done</td> <td>Security CI's <code>security-checks</code> job runs the hardened-XML / banned-pattern check (<code>check_banned_patterns</code>) and the static security invariant suites: verified TLS (<code>test_net_tls</code>), secret redaction / no-plaintext-secret diagnostics (<code>test_diagnostics</code>), XML-bomb hardening (<code>test_safe_xml</code>), zip decompression caps (<code>test_safe_archive</code>), the Python sandbox policy (<code>test_python_sandbox</code>), and the OCR argument allowlist (<code>test_ocr</code>). Dependency vulnerability auditing (<code>pip-audit --strict</code>) and the SBOM run in the adjacent job. The gate runs both as a CLI (<code>python -m quill.tools.module_size_budget</code>, non-zero exit on any violation) and as <code>tests/unit/tools/test_module_size_budget.py</code>, which the required <code>unit-tests</code> CI job runs as part of <code>pytest tests\unit</code>. The budget is decrease-only by construction — the documented <code>_comment</code>, the module docstring, and <code>test_every_budget_entry_at_least_matches_current_size_or_smaller_is_fine</code> make raising a number to paper over growth a self-inflicted failure. The ratchet is live: extracting <code>BrowseModeMixin</code>, <code>AiActionsMixin</code>, <code>settings_specs.py</code>, and <code>settings_normalizers.py</code> each forced the touched budgets <em>down</em> (e.g. <code>settings_registry.py</code> 933→158, <code>settings.py</code> 617→570), and the gate blocked those modules from shipping over budget until the code was extracted rather than the cap raised.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>GATE-12</td> <td>Strengthen AI assistant repository guidance</td> <td>Gates</td> <td>S</td> <td>Todo</td> <td>copilot-instructions and a new AGENTS.md describe architecture, strict zone, scoped mypy, accessibility, no-silent-network, the audit footguns, and the definition of done; Elevate the existing assistant transcript and Save/Open Session into a durable, navigable history: auto-saved sessions, continue-most-recent, browse-past, and fork/branch so a writer can try two rewrites of a section without losing state, then compare and resume. Turns form a tree by <code>parent_id</code>; the active branch tip is <code>current_turn_id</code>. <code>append_turn</code> adds a child of the tip and advances it; <code>branch_from</code>/<code>resume</code> move the tip back to an earlier turn so the next append creates a <em>sibling</em> branch — both rewrites are kept, never lost. <code>path_to</code>/<code>current_path</code> give the conversation along any branch; <code>branch_tips</code>/<code>branch_points</code> enumerate the leaves and forks; <code>compare_branches</code> finds the common ancestor and the turns unique to each side; <code>relabel_turn</code> names a branch for navigation. Tests cover the token heuristic, the over-budget compaction, recent-turn preservation, the too-few-turns and failed/blank-summary no-op paths.</td> </tr> <tr> <td>AI-24</td> <td>Language-agnostic stdio/JSON boundary for external engines</td> <td>AI</td> <td>M</td> <td>Done</td> <td>Derived from Pi's RPC/JSON integration design (see <code>docs/planning/pi.md</code>), and the architectural keystone for adopting any non-Python engine from a Python app. Define one consented, off-by-default pattern for QUILL to drive an external engine over a local subprocess speaking JSONL or MCP on stdio — spawned on demand, covered by the GATE-9 egress audit, with a clean unavailable path. This is the same boundary the Accessibility Agents work (<code>docs/planning/aa.md</code>) needs for its optional Node backend, so building it once de-risks both. Adopt the pattern, not the package. <strong>Delivered:</strong> <code>quill/core/ai/external_engine.py</code> is a complete, wx-free, strict-typed boundary. A master consent switch and a per-engine <code>enabled</code> flag are both <strong>off by default</strong> and persist under <code><app data>/ai/external-engines.json</code>. <code>probe_engine</code> decides availability with a human reason (master off, engine off, no command, missing program); <code>run_request</code> spawns the configured program on demand, writes one JSONL request line to stdin, reads one JSONL response from stdout, and maps every ordinary failure (disabled, missing executable, non-zero exit, invalid JSON, timeout, engine-reported <code>error</code>) to a structured <code>EngineResult</code> with <code>ok</code>/<code>unavailable</code>/<code>error</code> — it never raises for the expected failure modes, giving callers the required clean unavailable path. The subprocess runner is injectable, so the boundary is fully tested (10 tests) without spawning real processes. The boundary is local-only (pipes, no sockets); QUILL opens no network connection, so it adds no new site to the GATE-9 <code>urlopen</code>/<code>urlretrieve</code> egress inventory, and the off-by-default consent gate is the structural control. ruff + strict mypy clean. <strong>UI wired:</strong> the consent and command configuration now live in the registry-driven Settings home (no separate dialog): the AI page carries an off-by-default "Allow external engines" master checkbox plus an "External engine name"/"External engine command" pair and an "Enable this external engine" checkbox, persisted on OK via <code>set_external_engines_enabled</code> and <code>configure_engine</code> (a wx-free helper that turns the free-text command box into a token tuple with <code>shlex</code> and saves an <code>EngineConfig</code>). <code>list_engine_ids</code> and <code>configure_engine</code> are strict-typed and covered by core tests; the Settings integration is pinned by source-contract tests asserting the master/command controls and the persist-on-OK wiring, and the dialog-contract and public-surface guards stay green. No concrete external engine ships by design (adopt the pattern, not the package), but the consent gate, persistence, runtime boundary, and the Settings UI to enable an engine and configure its command are all complete and tested, so this row is Done.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr /> <h2 id="part-iv-the-combined-accessibility-suite-glow-and-bits-whisperer">Part IV: The combined accessibility suite (GLOW and BITS Whisperer)</h2> <p>QUILL does not exist alone. It sits beside two sibling products built for the same audience, and there is a rare opportunity to fuse them into a single, coherent, best-in-class accessibility suite rather than three overlapping apps. This part defines how to bring GLOW (document accessibility audit and fix) and BITS Whisperer (audio transcription) into QUILL as first-class, deeply integrated capabilities, what to keep, what to drop, and what shared foundation makes it durable.</p> <p>The strategic case: all three products share a mission (do excellent work for blind and low-vision people), a stack (Python and wxPython, accessibility-first, local-first), and an audience. Three separate apps mean three menus to learn, three update mechanisms, three places for a document to live, and triplicated engineering. One suite, with QUILL as the writing and editing home, GLOW as its accessibility engine, and BITS Whisperer as its transcription engine, is simpler for users and far more powerful: write, transcribe, audit, fix, and publish in one place, by keyboard and voice, with one set of conventions.</p> <h3 id="19-glow-integration-make-quill-accessibility-native">19. GLOW integration: make QUILL accessibility-native</h3> <blockquote> <p>The full, step-by-step 1.0 execution plan for this section (Tier 2 scope, sequenced after Tier 4) — the three-repo layout (<code>s:\code\quill-glow-core</code>, <code>s:\code\glow</code>, and QUILL), the ordered GLOW-0 through GLOW-7 work, the definition of done, and the risk register — lives in <a href="glow.md">glow.md</a> under <code>docs/planning/</code>. This section is the narrative; <a href="glow.md">glow.md</a> is the build sheet, and the two must stay in step.</p> </blockquote> <p>QUILL already contains <code>quill/core/glow.py</code>, a text-level GLOW audit and fix surface (generic link text, plain-language lint, audit and fix reports for the selection or document) wired to commands such as <code>tools.glow_fix_document</code> and <code>tools.glow_fix_selection</code>. Separately, GLOW is a full document-accessibility platform (a VS Code agent toolkit, a desktop app, and a web app) enforcing ACB Large Print, APH, WCAG 2.2 AA, and Microsoft Accessibility Checker rules across Word, Excel, PowerPoint, PDF, EPUB, HTML, and Markdown, with audit, auto-fix, template generation, and conversion. The shared library <code>quill-glow-core</code> already exposes a stable host-facing API (<code>audit_by_extension</code>, <code>fix_by_extension</code>, <code>convert_to_markdown</code>, <code>get_component_versions</code>) with a dispatch core, a safe no-op fallback, and a GLOW backend adapter.</p> <p>The plan: adopt <code>quill-glow-core</code> as the single shared engine so QUILL's in-editor GLOW and the GLOW desktop and web apps audit and fix by exactly the same rules, with one place to improve them.</p> <p>Where the code lives (for the implementer): the shared engine is the <code>quill-glow-core</code> repo at <code>s:\code\quill-glow-core</code> (package <code>quill_glow_core</code>, public API in <code>src/quill_glow_core/services.py</code>: <code>configure_default_services</code>, <code>audit_by_extension</code>, <code>fix_by_extension</code>, <code>convert_to_markdown</code>, <code>get_component_versions</code>, plus <code>from_glow_backend</code>, which bridges to the canonical engine <code>acb_large_print_core</code>). The full GLOW platform repo is <code>s:\code\glow</code>. Note: <code>s:\code\glow-7.0.0</code> is a stale snapshot and should be ignored; do not read or modify it. This GLOW work therefore spans up to three repos — QUILL (this repo, the presentation layer), <code>quill-glow-core</code> (the shared contract), and <code>glow</code> (the rule engine) — so changes must be coordinated, each committed in its own repo, and the shared API kept stable.</p> <p>Cross-repo prerequisite for GLOW-1 step 1: the <code>s:\code\glow</code> repo currently has failing CI/tests. Before QUILL depends on <code>quill-glow-core</code> (GLOW-1), the <code>glow</code> repo's failures must be diagnosed and fixed and its suite brought green, so QUILL builds on a stable engine rather than inheriting breakage. This is the first task of GLOW-1 and is tracked in the GLOW-1 acceptance criteria.</p> <ul> <li>Depend on the shared core. Replace QUILL's bespoke text-level checks with calls into <code>quill-glow-core</code> (<code>configure_default_services</code> then <code>audit_by_extension</code> and <code>fix_by_extension</code>), keeping QUILL's friendly in-editor reports as the presentation layer. When the GLOW backend is present, QUILL gets the full ACB, APH, WCAG, and MSAC rule sets; when it is absent, the safe no-op fallback keeps QUILL fully functional. See GLOW-1.</li> <li>Audit and fix by structure, not just text. Today QUILL audits plain text, Markdown, and HTML. Extend it through the shared core to audit and fix the structured formats QUILL already reads (DOCX, PPTX, XLSX, PDF, EPUB) so a user can open a real document and run a full accessibility audit in place. See GLOW-2, IO-1.</li> <li>An in-editor accessibility report that reads beautifully. Present GLOW findings as a navigable, screen-reader-pageable list grouped by severity, each with a one-key jump to the location, a plain-language explanation, and (where fixable) a reviewable apply-and-undo. This is the same surface the Accessibility agent (AGENT-1) drives. See GLOW-3, AGENT-1, AI-7.</li> <li>Standards profiles in QUILL. Surface GLOW's profiles (ACB 2025 Baseline, APH Submission, Combined Strict) as a setting so a user can choose the rigor that fits their work, with the active profile shown in every report for traceable evidence. See GLOW-4, SET-1.</li> <li>One-key publish to accessible output. Reuse GLOW's conversion chain (MarkItDown plus Pandoc, with LibreOffice-assisted pre-conversion and PyMuPDF table preservation) so QUILL can export clean, accessible Word, HTML, EPUB, and PDF with announced results. This realizes FEAT-17 on a proven engine. See GLOW-5, FEAT-17.</li> <li>Shared versioning and telemetry. Use <code>get_component_versions</code> and the startup telemetry so QUILL can show which accessibility engine and rule version is active, keeping the honesty principle. See GLOW-6.</li> </ul> <p>What to keep lightweight in QUILL: QUILL should not absorb GLOW's web app, its branding-profile deployment machinery, or its template-generation server flows. QUILL consumes the shared core; the GLOW desktop and web apps remain the heavyweight authoring and batch surfaces. The boundary is clean: shared rules and fixers in <code>quill-glow-core</code>, three thin presentation layers on top.</p> <h3 id="20-bits-whisperer-integration-transcription-becomes-a-quill-superpower">20. BITS Whisperer integration: transcription becomes a QUILL superpower</h3> <blockquote> <p>Status (2026-06-02): deferred to <strong>QUILL 2.0</strong>. BITS Whisperer is not part of the 1.0 milestone; its build order lives in Tier 5 (Part V). In the shipping 1.0 application the entire suite is held back behind the locked-off <code>core.bw_whisperer</code> feature flag — the <strong>BITS Whisperer</strong> menu is not appended to the menu bar, its palette commands are gated out via the <code>bw_*</code> feature dependencies, and the first-run Startup Wizard skips the BITS Whisperer onboarding step — so no transcription surface reaches a 1.0 user. The narrative below is the 2.0 integration vision; the <code>quill/core/bw_speech.py</code> and <code>quill/core/bw_providers.py</code> scaffolding is retained as the 2.0 foundation.</p> </blockquote> <p>QUILL already contains <code>quill/core/bw_speech.py</code>, a speech-model manager that mirrors a subset of BITS Whisperer (faster-whisper model specs, hardware eligibility, a model manager, provider status), exposed through a "BITS Whisperer" menu group (Speech Model Manager, Provider Center, Use Recommended, and so on). BITS Whisperer itself is a mature, accessibility-first transcription app: 18 providers (cloud and on-device), 14 Whisper models, AI translation and summarization, live microphone transcription, speaker diarization, a watch folder, scheduled transcription, do-not-disturb, a plugin system, seven export formats, and a setup wizard, all WCAG-adapted with a menu-first, screen-reader-first design.</p> <p>The opportunity is large: a writer who can transcribe an interview or a lecture and immediately edit, audit, and publish it, all in one accessible app, has something no mainstream editor offers. The plan is to bring BITS Whisperer's transcription engine into QUILL as a first-class "Transcribe" capability, reusing BW's provider and model layer rather than reimplementing it.</p> <p>What to bring into QUILL (high value):</p> <ul> <li>Transcribe to a document. Add a Transcribe command that takes an audio or video file (or a folder) and produces a QUILL document with the transcript, ready to edit, audit with GLOW, and publish. Reuse BW's provider abstraction and faster-whisper model manager (the <code>bw_speech.py</code> foundation already present). See BW-1.</li> <li>Local-first providers by default. Surface BW's on-device providers (local Whisper via faster-whisper, Vosk, Parakeet, Windows Speech, Azure Embedded) as the default, with cloud providers strictly opt-in and consented, matching QUILL's no-silent-network rule. See BW-2, AI-5.</li> <li>Live dictation into the editor. Bring BW's live microphone transcription in as an accessible "dictate into the document" mode with clear start, stop, and status announcements, complementing QUILL's existing dictation. See BW-3.</li> <li>Speaker labels and clean structure. Use BW's diarization to produce well-structured, speaker-labeled transcripts that QUILL can then clean with the Cleanup agent. See BW-4, AGENT-2.</li> <li>AI translation and summarization on the transcript, through QUILL's own consented AI layer rather than a parallel one. See BW-5, AI-8.</li> <li>Watch folder and batch. Offer BW's watch-folder and batch transcription as an optional power feature, announced non-intrusively, reusing QUILL's existing watch-folder pattern. See BW-6, FEAT-9.</li> <li>A unified Provider and Model Center. Consolidate BW's provider and model management with QUILL's AI model and connection management into one accessible Settings home, so a user manages all engines (writing AI, transcription providers, speech models) in one place. See BW-7, MENU-1, SET-1.</li> </ul> <p>What to drop or de-scope from the standalone BITS Whisperer plan once integrated:</p> <ul> <li>Retire the duplicate application shell. The separate BW main window, tray icon, setup wizard, and updater are not needed inside QUILL; QUILL provides the shell, onboarding, and update path. Keep BW as a library, not a second app. See BW-8.</li> <li>Drop duplicated subsystems. BW's own settings store, watch folder, plugin manager, registration and licensing, beta service, and Copilot chat panel should defer to QUILL's equivalents rather than ship twice. Consolidate to one of each. See BW-8.</li> <li>Reconsider breadth of cloud providers. Eighteen providers is a maintenance load; in the suite, lead with the strong on-device set plus a small, well-supported cloud selection, and treat the long tail as optional plugins rather than core. See BW-9.</li> <li>Unify export. QUILL plus GLOW already cover accessible export (Word, HTML, EPUB, PDF, Markdown); transcript-specific formats (SRT, VTT) become QUILL export presets rather than a separate BW exporter. See BW-10, FEAT-17.</li> </ul> <p>The combined-suite outcome: one accessible app where a blind or low-vision user can transcribe spoken audio, write and edit the result, audit and fix it to ACB, APH, and WCAG standards, and publish accessible output, entirely by keyboard and voice, with local-first privacy and one consistent set of conventions. That is a genuinely category-defining product, and it reuses two existing, proven engines instead of building from scratch.</p> <h3 id="21-shared-foundation-for-the-suite">21. Shared foundation for the suite</h3> <ul> <li>One shared accessibility core. <code>quill-glow-core</code> is the single source of audit and fix rules for QUILL, GLOW desktop, and GLOW web. See GLOW-1.</li> <li>One transcription engine. BITS Whisperer's provider and model layer becomes a library consumed by QUILL (and still usable standalone if desired). See BW-1, BW-8.</li> <li>One set of conventions and gates. The quality-gate ladder (Part III) and the accessibility non-negotiables apply across the suite, so all three surfaces meet the same bar. See GATE-2.</li> <li>One identity for the user. Shared secret storage, shared update path, and a single Settings home reduce cognitive load and duplicated engineering. See SET-1, BW-7.</li> </ul> <h4 id="211-new-backlog-items-for-the-combined-suite">21.1 New backlog items for the combined suite</h4> <p>These extend the section 14 tracker. The GLOW family (GLOW-1 through GLOW-8) has a dedicated execution plan in <a href="glow.md">glow.md</a>; keep both in step when any GLOW item changes scope or status.</p> <table> <thead> <tr> <th>ID</th> <th>Item</th> <th>Area</th> <th>Size</th> <th>Status</th> <th>Acceptance criteria</th> </tr> </thead> <tbody> <tr> <td>GLOW-1</td> <td>Adopt quill-glow-core as the shared engine</td> <td>Suite</td> <td>M</td> <td>In progress</td> <td>Step 1 (glow repo, not yet verified): in <code>s:\code\glow</code>, the consumed desktop core (<code>acb_large_print</code> / <code>acb_large_print_core</code>, the target of <code>from_glow_backend</code>) is already green (308 tests); fix the failing Flask web suite (<code>acb_large_print_web</code>: the <code>/guide/</code> content string, branding injection, and form-POST tests) and reconcile the version sweep (VERSION 8.0.0 vs README vs TODO.md), committing in the <code>glow</code> repo so the whole engine is green.
